  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ce2ce9b2-09b8-47d3-a7f6-b74a19d9108c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText6093979060021840196" style="display:none"><i>Never, ever cry...</i><br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Eureka won't let anyone close enough to feel her pain. After her mother was killed in a freak accident, the things she used to love hold no meaning. She wants to escape, but one thing holds her back: Ander, the boy who is everywhere she goes, whose turquoise eyes are like the ocean. And then Eureka uncovers an ancient tale of romance and heartbreak, about a girl who cried an entire continent into the sea. Suddenly her mother's death and Ander's appearance seem connected, and her life takes on dark undercurrents that don't make sense. Can everything you love be washed away?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15987890201018320982">EDITED 06/19/2013: James Dashner has apologized via Twitter. Thank you for all your support, everyone. <3 /edit<br/><br/>EDITED 06/18/2013: <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380561159i/3115662.png' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> O_o /edit<br/><br/>This book is bad. He held all the cards. Eureka’s role in the relationship seemed merely to be al</span>
  <span id="freeText15987890201018320982" style="display:none">EDITED 06/19/2013: James Dashner has apologized via Twitter. Thank you for all your support, everyone. &lt;3 /edit<br><br>EDITED 06/18/2013: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380561159i/3115662.png" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> O_o /edit<br><br>This book is bad. Hence, my review is very long. *thumbs-up*<br><br>I have included as many quotes as possible to illustrate my points.<br><br><b>Characters</b>:<br><br>Eureka (that name -__-;) is so utterly passive she even remarks on it herself: “Trust was mutual, and that was the problem with her and Ander. He held all the cards. Eureka’s role in the relationship seemed merely to be alarmed.” (p. 311) She also goes through long internal monologues like this one:<br><blockquote>“Eureka’s life was in chaos. She was on the brink of being kicked out of the house she hated living in. She hadn’t been going to school. She was alienated from all her friends and was following birds through the predawn bayou to meet elderly psychics. How was she supposed to know if <i>now</i> was Diana’s mystical <i>when</i>?” (p. 314)</blockquote><br>All the negative sides of her character (being a sucky all-around friend to Cat and Brooks, withdrawing from every type of social contact except with Cat, Ander, Brooks and Madame Blavatsky, stereotyping practically every single female character she encounters) could’ve been redeemed were it not for the fact that she shows no growth. Even when she has a fight with Brooks and he tells her everything you as the reader are dying to tell her (“‘You keep Cat around because she doesn’t notice when you tune her out. You can’t stand anyone in your family. You’re certain every therapist you go to is an idiot. You’ve pushed away all of Evangeline [their school] because there’s no way anyone could ever understand what you’ve been through.’” p. 161), his words are written off because later it’s explained that he was being possessed by an evil Atlantean, so she doesn’t have to change!<br><br>There are a lot of female characters.<br><br>Cat is Eureka’s best friend the way the protag of Jodi Picoult’s <i>Between the Lines</i> had a best friend: they make for warm fuzzy scenes together, but in the end, Cat is really not essential to the story.<br><br>Rhoda is Eureka’s father’s new wife who is so evil and unloving that she is a completely unrealistic caricature. Here, a quote of the type of things she says to Eureka:<br><blockquote>“‘It looks like you were just bumming around with Brooks. You know it’s a school night. What happened with the therapist? I hope you didn’t do anything to embarrass me.” (p. 102)<br><br>“‘As long as you live in my house, you follow my rules.’” (p.187)<br><br><br>“‘Don’t tell me you forgot you were watching the twins? Your dad’s at work and I’m delivering the keynote at the dean’s luncheon.”<br>“I made plans with Brooks.”<br>“Rearrange them.” Rhoda tilted her head and frowned. “We were doing so well.” (p. 336)</blockquote><br>Maya Cayce is the girl who wants to get with Brooks. Eureka says Maya hates her: “She was a senior, a roller skater, a rumored Wiccan, a transcender of all cliques, a contralto in the choir, a state-champion equestrian (<i>ed note</i>: omg, jealous. I want to be a state-champion equestrian), and she hated Eureka Boudreaux." (p. 68) Is that enough reason for Eureka to hate her back? Guess so if you’re intent on making every other female character in your book seem like they’re out to destroy your protag. But personally, all the aforementioned description sounds like she would make a fabulous friend.<br><br>The female-hating goes on: we get a description of “arduously identical cheerleaders” (p. 169), and girls described thusly: “never has she ever considered wearing pants that didn’t show her thong… never has she ever left the house without a pound of makeup.” (p. 277) Eureka’s therapist says: “‘You will wake up at forty with no husband, no children and no career if you don’t learn to engage with the world” (p. 193), giving Eureka even more reason to dismiss her (“The only person who understood Eureka was scattered across the sea.” p. 193). Does a therapist actually speak like that and retain her job? Does a stepmother sound as evil as Rhoda, for that matter?<br><br>Even BFF Cat gets slammed: “‘You think everything is about sex.’” (p. 167) Never mind Maya Cayce—she’s portrayed as a slut with every breath she takes: “She was also the only person whose Evangeline slacks fit her body like an obscene glove.” And later on the same page: “He [Brooks] caught Maya when she flung her body at his in an X-rated hug.” (p. 207)<br><br>And here’s Eureka commenting on the one woman who she believes is genuine: “Aileen was the sweetest woman in New Iberia—and the only woman Eureka knew whose sweetness wasn’t saccharine.” (p. 231) SNARK: Really, Eureka? The <i>only</i> woman in the whole state who is genuinely sweet? /SNARK<br><br>Another commonly recurring descriptor is the focus on people’s looks, and women’s in particular in relation to their worth. Eureka has an aunt named Maureen, who she compares to her mother Diana: “Diana had inherited a truckload more class; Maureen got Sugar’s ample breasts and wore dangerously low-cut blouses to show her heirlooms off.” (p. 107) Eureka actually thinks that the biggest difference between her mother and her aunt is that her mother is beautiful. Not her personality. Not her loving nature or generous character or anything else: “Studying her aunt across the table, Eureka realized that the main difference between the sisters was that Eureka’s mother was beautiful. You could look at Maureen and see Diana gone wrong. She was a cruel parody.” (p. 109)<br><br>No mention of Rhoda is complete without talking about her faded beauty:<br><blockquote>“She was really pretty, and sometimes Eureka could even see it—when Rhoda was sleeping, or in the trance of watching her children, the rare moments when her face relaxed. But most of the time, Rhoda just looked late for something. She wore this orangey lipstick, which had worn off while she was instructing tonight’s business class at the university. Little tributaries of faded orange ran down the creases of her lips.” (p. 101)</blockquote><br>Even her father is gorgeous: “His name was Trenton Michel Boudreaux the Third. He had a defining slimness that he’d passed onto all three of his kids. He was tall with a wiry, dark blond hair and a smile that could charm a copperhead. You’d have to be blind not to notice how women flirted with him. Maybe Dad was trying to be blind to it—he always closed his eyes when he laughed off their advances.” (p. 79)<br><br>And Anders is the hottest guy Eureka has ever seen. <b>She actually says this guys.</b> “He was the hottest guy she’d ever yelled at. He might have been the hottest boy she’d ever seen.” (p. 34) Dear authors: it’s possible to swoon over a less-than-average-looking guy, you know. <br><br>The romance. Brooks and Eureka I was okay with; the confusion after their first kiss was well-done, especially when taking into account the fact that he was possessed by an Atlantean. (This doesn’t excuse the fact that this basically allows Eureka to not grow as a character, of course.) But with Anders, Eureka goes from feeling understandable butterflies in his presence to rightfully feeling weirded out by their lopsided relationship and his stalker-ish behaviour to abruptly loving him because suddenly they hug, he spills all these secrets and everything’s intimate:<br><blockquote>”Ander’s hold on her had the kind of depth she’d felt with only a few people before. Diana, Dad, Brooks, Cat—Eureka could count them. It was a depth that suggested profound affection, a depth that bordered on love. She expected to want to pull away, but she leaned closer.<br>His open hands came to rest against her back. His shoulders spanned hers like a protective shield, which made her think of the thunderstone. He tilted his head to cradle hers against his chest. Through his T-shirt, she could hear his heart throbbing. She loved the sound it made.<br>She closed her eyes and knew that Ander’s eyes were closed, too. Their closed eyes cast a heavy silence on the room. Eureka suddenly felt she was in the safest place on the earth and she knew she had been wrong about him.” (p. 369 – 370)</blockquote><br>So… should we dissect that last quote there? (WARNING: SNARK.) “She loved the sound it made.” Every heartbeat sounds the same. “Their closed eyes cast a heavy silence on the room.” No, your <i>silence</i> cast a heavy silence on the room. “…the kind of depth she’d felt with only a few people.” Yeah, that’s normal. It’s called love, and most people do not experience profound love with more than a few people, so that’s not anything special. “She knew she had been wrong about him.” What, because he hugs you nicely? No.<br>/snark<br><br>The sudden intimacy is abrupt and makes the kissing supremely unromantic, though Lauren Kate’s kiss scenes are pretty good. And Ander says: “‘Every moment of your life, I have fallen more deeply in love with you.’” (p. 394) Eureka responds by trying “to transmit the words she couldn’t find with a kiss” (p. 394), which smacks of the dangerous message “If he loves you, then that’s a good enough reason to love him.”<br><br>ALSO, this is how Eureka describes his eyes: "... his eyes were turquoise, like the ocean in Miami, and thus made her think of Diana. She sensed sadness in their depths, like shadows in the sea." (p.33)<br><br>She "sensed" sadness. Like "shadows in the sea".<br><br>*insert jawdrop GIF here*<br><br><b>Pacing</b><br><br>With every paranormal novel in which the protag discovers new powers/worlds/secrets in a contemporary setting, there must inevitably be an adjustment period where everyone related to this discovery goes through the process of “holy shit, what?” Acceptance doesn’t happen overnight.<br><br>However, this book spends a bloated amount of time setting up its secrets, and not enough time revealing it. Eureka meets Anders in at least five different locations in short, choppy scenes when three fully fleshed scenes would’ve been fine. We see Eureka in normal locales like school parties and track meets, but these do nothing to advance the story; they seem intended to develop character. Yeah, no. (Sorry, no quote to back this point up; I’d have to quote an entire chapter + context.) Overall, this 440 page novel doesn’t distribute the passing of time evenly or even with coherence. This means we’ve guessed everything before Eureka, but then the pace is forced to move far too rapidly after the grand reveal; Ander talks about going to Turkey, the country, as if that’s feasible with Eureka’s parental situation???:<br><blockquote>“‘The last I heard, he [Solon, a Seedbearer] was in Turkey.’ He [Ander] spun to face Eureka, eyes suddenly bright. ‘We could go there and track him down.’<br>Eureka laughed. ‘I doubt my Dad is going to let me up and go to Turkey.’<br>‘They’ll have to come with us,’ Ander said quickly. ‘All of your loved ones will. Otherwise my family would use your family to drag you back.’<br>Eureka stiffened. ‘You mean—’<br>He nodded. ‘They can justify killing a few in order to save many.’” (p. 395 – 396)</blockquote><br>In the confrontation between Ander and the Seedbearers (I’m sorry, that name just reminds me of a sperm bank), there was so much potential for themes of loyalty and family and choice. (“‘We raised you to be smarter than this. Did you not memorize the Chronicles? Do thousands years [sic] of history mean nothing to you? …Love has blinded you to your heritage.’” p. 418) No substance isn’t necessarily a bad thing, of course, so I’m not going to treat this as a knock against the book. More of a huge missed opportunity to add depth.<br><br><b>Setting</b><br><br>The setting is quite interesting (yay, three cheers for positive things!): it is set in New Iberia (as a Canadian I have no clue where that is, but didn’t hamper me from enjoying it) in a well-described bayou climate. The swamps, hurricanes and general wetness of the area translates well through the description-heavy scenes and also serve as a relatively realistic backdrop to the dramatic events of the climax.<br><br><b>Writing</b><br><br>Some decent showing, but LOTS of telling. Paragraphs upon paragraphs, occasionally. Flashbacks are also awkwardly inserted into the middle of conversations and real-time scenes. Transitions from one locale to another happen with no segue and often with a load of time passing in between.<br><br><b>Miscellaneous</b><br><br>Two women die in this novel—major characters whose deaths add shock value but little else. Why? Because they do not change the stakes of the story.<br><br>Madame Blavatsky is the stereotypical mystical psychic woman, ability to talk to her Abyssinian lovebirds and all. A few quotes:<br><blockquote>“‘There is no death, no life, either. Only congregation and dispersal.’” (p. 175)<br>“‘It might be dangerous,’ Blavatsky continued. ‘Knowledge is power; power corrupts. Corruption brings shame and ruin. Ignorance may not be bliss, but it is perhaps preferable to a life lived in shame. Do you agree?’” (p. 179)<br>“‘Nothing is real. There is only what we believe in and what we reject.’” (p. 293)<br>“‘Curiosity is a cunning paramour,’ the woman said. ‘He has me seduced as well.’” (p. 295)<br>“‘We believe is your destiny to go [sic],’ Madame Blavatsky said. ‘What happens once you’re there is up to you.’” (p. 297)</blockquote><br>I know I already said this, but Eureka goes through a LOT of angst. Have some more quotes:<br><br><blockquote>“Nothing Eureka could say would change the cruel rules of this house, which only ever applied to her. Her mind was on fire, but her eyes stayed downturned. She had better things to do than fight with the monsters across the table.” (p. 309)<br><br>“She heard Brooks buzzing something nasty in her ear about how Eureka was convinced all her therapists were stupid. This one really was!” (p. 191)</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15987890201018320982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer746139486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13209499112793591579"><br/><u>
  <b>ROUNDING UP TO 1.5 STARS.</b>
</u><br/><br/>*I won <i>Teardrop</i> through a goodreads giveaway.* <br/><br/>When i first saw the cover <br/><br/><a target='_blank' title='ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting' href='http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/855/2ilb.jpg/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383251167i/6459153.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a target='_blank' href='http://imageshack.us' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/><br/>i was a bit like this....<br/><br/><a href='http://pl.tinypic.com?ref=jaz3wg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383251167ra/6459154.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Isn't that one of the most beautiful and breathtaking covers ever?!<br/><br/>However, the actual book couldn't be more different. <br/><br/><a target='_blank' title='ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting' href='http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/854/r9vj.jpg/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383257480i/6462886.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a target='_blank' href='http://imageshack.us' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/><br/>17 year old Eureka never cries, not even at her own beloved mum's funeral, who died at a freak accident. Eureka was with her in that car when it happened, but the next thing she knows she's laying in the hospital bed. Why did she survive an</span>
  <span id="freeText13209499112793591579" style="display:none"><br><u>
  <b>ROUNDING UP TO 1.5 STARS.</b>
</u><br><br>*I won <i>Teardrop</i> through a goodreads giveaway.* <br><br>When i first saw the cover <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/855/2ilb.jpg/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383251167i/6459153.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>i was a bit like this....<br><br><a href="http://pl.tinypic.com?ref=jaz3wg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383251167ra/6459154.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Isn't that one of the most beautiful and breathtaking covers ever?!<br><br>However, the actual book couldn't be more different. <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/854/r9vj.jpg/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383257480i/6462886.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>17 year old Eureka never cries, not even at her own beloved mum's funeral, who died at a freak accident. Eureka was with her in that car when it happened, but the next thing she knows she's laying in the hospital bed. Why did she survive and not her mum? How?<br><br>The things she used to love hold no meaning anymore. She wants to escape. But then she meet Ander: The mysterious boy who is everywhere she goes, whose eyes take her breath away. <br><br>Then Eureka uncovers an ancient tale of romance, heartbreak and a city waiting beneath the waves. <b>Will it rise again</b>? <br><b>Is Eureka the key to restoration....or destruction?</b><br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/607/ksjo.jpg/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383257733i/6463116._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>First impressions are sometimes fetal in the book world</b>, in my occasion almost always. For those who don't know, or have yet to realize, <i>Teardrop</i> is the 1st book in <i>Lauren Kate's</i> new trilogy (she is the author of the 'best selling' Fallen series).<br>I have not read the <i>Fallen</i> series yet, so this was my first encounter with Mrs Kate, and i am <b>NOT IMPRESSED</b> to put it kindly. <br><br>There were so many bad things about <i>Teardrop</i>. I don't even know where to start. <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/27/dppa.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468727.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><u>
  <b>From the beginning</b>
</u> it's the guy's POV (Ander), and we can see that he has some serious stalker issues with Eureka. To me he seemed kinda...obsessed.<br><br><b>
  <i>'He has been watching her since before he or she could speak. They have never spoke. <br>She was his life.<br>He had to kill her.'</i>
</b><br><br>So Ander also has to choose between saving the world, or saving the girl. Guess what he chooses? <b>The.Girl.</b> Naturally.<br>That happens a lot in YA books, but i don't think the authors realize that <b>if the dude chooses the girl over the world, SHE WILL DIE ANYWAY? </b>Because if the world will be gone or something, she and everyone else will go down with it? <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/823/17cu.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468728.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><u>
  <b>The Characters</b>
</u><br><br><u>
  <b>Eureka:</b>
</u> I thought i'll very much connect with her, it seemed we had quite a bit in common. But nope. Truth be told i didn't care if she died the next page. I didn't like her. I could not connect with her.<br><b>I thought she was a shallow and very undeveloped protagonist</b>.<br><br><u>
  <b>Ander:</b>
</u> Excuse me - i still don't know who the fuck you are?? WHAT IS THE POINT OF YOUR EXISTENCE? Like...<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/692/a63d.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468729.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>I didn't really learn anything about Ander. I didn't like him, though at times i admit he could be rather...sweet. <br><br><u>
  <b>Brooks</b>
</u>: I think he is my favorite character. Brooks is Eureka's oldest and bestest friend. He was supportive, very charming, fun and just lovable! I wouldn't mind if someone put him in a box, wrapped him up and gave to me as a present *cough*.<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/812/29e5.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468730.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><u>
  <b>The Romance</b>
</u><br> <br>One of what seems like many reasons this book was a 1 star read. <br>This definitely makes the top 5 most <b>cliche</b>, <b>unrealistic</b> and <b>ridiculous</b> love triangles/romance books i have read. <br> <br><b>
  <i>'His tongue traced the tip of her tongue. (...) She arched her back. <br>"This feels-" he said. <br>She nodded "so right". </i>
</b><br> <br><b>*TINY SPOILER ALERT (nothing important)* </b><br>That quote is when Eureka and Brooks had their 'first kiss'. <br>They 'feel' its right, yeah? But guess what. Like a day or 2 later Eureka is all like 'it didn't feel right anyway' when Ander is near by. <br>And then she changes again to the 'feels right' mood. <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/13/lyp.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468731.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>The romance was <b>EXTREMELY</b> rushed. She went from one guy to the next before i could even say 'Knife and your head bitch'. I <b>could not feel ANY chemistry</b> either between her and Ander or Brooks.<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/96/tt10.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468732.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>I HATE when the authors think their audience isn't as smart as they are</b>. It created an impression like this was the case with <i>Teardrop</i>, as i had, like, 95% of the twist/plot figured out from the middle half of the book. <br><br><b>IT WAS PREDICTABLE!</b><br> I felt like the author either thought no one would be as smart as her to figure it out, or she really thought it was unpredictable and had some real 'twists' in the story that would shock her readers to the bones.<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/199/0tby.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468733.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><i>Teardrop</i> is a <b>big book</b>, guys. Possesses <b>over 400 pages</b>. And i promise you - <b>NEARLY. NOTHING. HAPPENED</b>! <br>It was just dragging on insignificantly. I was FIGHTING with my self to keep on reading and not DNF it so i was put out of my misery. But i finished. Skipped most of the last couple of pages...but finished nonetheless.<br><br> Do you know what the book was the ENTIRE way? <b>CONFUSING</b>.<br> I did not, and still don't understand about 80% of what happened and about 90% of it all in general. <br><br><b>It was WEIRD! </b><br><br>Every chapter i'm all like...<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/543/asx.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468734.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><u>
  <b>Overall...</b>
</u><br><br>I'm disappointed. <br><br>The only good thing about this book were the ever so tiny glimpses of mythology (which i LOVED with all my heart).<br><br>I expected everything opposite what i really got.<br><br>However, i must give Mrs Kate some credit, as it is hard to write a very good book.<br><br><b>BUT...</b><br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/824/rurn.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383267296ra/6468735.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><i>Sincerely - The Critic.</i> <br><br> <b></b><br><i></i><br><u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><blockquote></blockquote></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_633101630" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633101630" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633101630?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=tstl">tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=why-do-i-hate-myself">why-do-i-hate-myself</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633101630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13768541139727261921">I'm grateful for many things in life, including the fact that most of YA fiction is in fact, fiction. <b>Because thankfully, my fate and that of the world will never rest in the hands of a teenaged boy who thinks with his dick.</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>The choice was simpler than that:<br/>Save the world, or save the girl.</i>
</blockquote>Guess which choice the boy makes? Ding ding ding, winner winner chicken dinner. <b>Because pussy will win out against humanity and common sense every single time</b>.<br/><br/>This book was not bad. It was simply generic. T</span>
  <span id="freeText13768541139727261921" style="display:none">I'm grateful for many things in life, including the fact that most of YA fiction is in fact, fiction. <b>Because thankfully, my fate and that of the world will never rest in the hands of a teenaged boy who thinks with his dick.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>The choice was simpler than that:<br />Save the world, or save the girl.</i>
</blockquote>Guess which choice the boy makes? Ding ding ding, winner winner chicken dinner. <b>Because pussy will win out against humanity and common sense every single time</b>.<br /><br />This book was not bad. It was simply generic. The premise behind it is one of the lost island of Atlantis, and honestly, that wasn't even a major part of the story. The mythology and what was supposed to be the major plotline in the book---that of Eureka and her mysterious destiny---was simply overshadowed by a large amount of angst, drama, and copious amounts of insta-love, love triangles, and stalking.<br /><br />This book just blends in with every other YA contemporary fantasy/paranormal works out there. The plot behind it is a little different, more refreshing than that of your generic angel/fairies/vampires/werewolves/witches/whatever, but the premise behind it is the same. As are the characters. Simply put, I could not pick Eureka out of a lineup of 100 other YA PNRs heroines out there. <b>She is a heroine made from a cookie cutter</b>.<br /><br /><u>The Plot</u>: We start off knowing a boy, Ander, has been watching over Eureka her whole life. She and her mother are driving across a bridge, they should be dead before crossing it. Against his family's wishes, against common sense...Ander saves the girl. Her mother, Diana dies. Over a year later, Eureka is still in mourning, recovering from a suicide attempt, all the while pushing away everyone she loves. She meets Ander as he rear-ends her, leaving no insurance information, getting her in trouble (nice). All of a sudden, Ander starts popping up all over the damn place. Her best friend Brooks is acting strange. Her mother leaves her some mysterious objects and a notebook in an indecipherable language. What is the mystery behind Ander? What does the notebook say? <b>Will Eureka ever stop sulking? Who will turn out to be Eureka's love of her life?</b><br /><br />Oh, and there's something about Atlantis.<br /><br /><u>The setting &amp; the writing</u>: <b>No complaints with either.</b> I loved the Louisiana setting, and the writing is solidly in line with the story. It is not spectacular, and it tends towards the overdramatic where Eureka is concerned, but it was easy to read, and never overly purple prosy. The writing made the book an easy, quick read.<br /><br /><u>The characters</u>: Underwhelming.<br /><br />Eureka: I'm glad she is not special in an "Why, little ole me? Pshaw!" sort of way. I'm glad she doesn't mention how ordinary she is only to have half the school fall in love with her. I'm glad she is an average, sullen teenager. <b>I'm glad she has her flaws, but there is nothing in her personality, that makes me empathize with her, that makes me like her, that makes her stand out. Eureka is bland.</b> The only thing that distinguishes her from other heroines I've read is her name. A book can be made or broken based on the strengths of the characters and their development, their complexity, and Eureka is dull and stereotypical.<br /><br />I understand her sullenness. I understand her grief. I wanted her to grow from it. I wanted her to grow beyond that. I wanted her to become extraordinary, to distinguish herself, to reach out from beyond her grief and anger. Eureka does not reach any sort of high standards for me. She is Bella Swan, comatose with sorrow after Edward leaves. She does not grow. She gives up before she even tries.<br /><br />The only thing that makes her feel anything is a boy she can barely remember meeting. That angers me so much. <b>It doesn't bother me that Eureka tries to commit suicide, I understand it, I sympathize with it. It bothers me that she finds nothing in life worthwhile, not her friends, not her old hobbies, not her family...until she meets a boy.</b> That is so utterly foolish to me. Eureka is an atrocious friend. She is a terrible daughter. I just about stood up in my chair and cheered when her best friend finally confronted Eureka about all her bullshittery.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You keep Cat around because she doesn’t notice when you tune her out. You can’t stand anyone in your family...You’re certain every therapist you go to is an idiot. You’ve pushed away all of Evangeline because there’s no way anyone could ever understand what you’ve been through.” He stopped pacing and looked straight at her. “Then there’s me.”<br />Eureka’s chest ached as if he’d punched her in the heart. “What about you?”<br />“You use me.”<br />“No.”<br />“I’m not your friend. I’m a sounding board for your anxiety and depression.”</i>
</blockquote>I really could not have analyzed Eureka and her apathy towards life any better than her best friend, Brooks, did. Needless to say, Brooks is my favorite character in the book, by far.<br /><br />Ander: Your typical teenaged stalker. <b>Ander makes Edward Cullen seem like a nice, personable young man who gives the woman he loves such a thing as "personal space."</b> Ander is a fucking stalker, man. He even refers to himself as one. What do you call someone who's been watching Eureka for her entire life, literally since the moment she was born. What do you call someone who shows up EVERYWHERE Eureka happens to be?<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“That’s why you never knew about me. I have watched you since you were born, but you never saw me until I wanted you to—the day I hit your car. I’ve been with you every day for the past seventeen years. I watched you learn to walk, to tie your shoes, to play the guitar”—he swallowed—“to kiss. I watched you get your ears pierced, fail your driver’s test, and win your first cross-country race.”</i>
</blockquote><b>The rest of the characters are tropes</b>. We have the bitter, past-her-prime bitch of a stepmother who is out to get Eureka every chance she gets. If you look up "evil stepmother," in the dictionary, you will find Rhoda's picture. There is no redeeming quality for her, none. Rhoda is so pure one-dimensional bitchiness that it is unbelievable. I have more sympathy for her father, who redefines "spineless." He cannot stand up to his first wife, Diana. He can barely hold his own with his second wife, Rhoda. Forget about dealing with his teenaged daughter...Eureka's dad is a spineless shell of a man. I find him a sad, tragic character.<br /><br /><b>The other prominent females in the book are whores against the virginal goodness of sweet, innocent hardly-been-kissed Eureka.</b> We have Cat, the awesome token black best friend, who is---duh---hypersexual, because black girls aren't already sexualized enough in the media these days. Cat slips onto a minidress that she keeps in her trunk to walk across a track field. She flirts with anything that has a penis. Cat sexualizes everything, despite her prowess on the track, despite her 2390 SAT scores. I am so sick of the oversexualized best friend. And then we have Maya, a roller derby Amazon of a goddess, who is a whore and a bitch, who hangs onto Brooks (like he's completely virginal), who hates Eureka for no reason at all. <b>Of course, Maya is the ho, and Brooks is just simply the poor unwilling lad whose leg she just happens to be leg-humping. Brooks is completely innocent in all of this. Fucking please.</b><br /><br /><u>The Romance</u>: Insta-love. Love Triangle. Adultery.<br /><br />The love triangle &amp; cheating is considerably less annoying than the head-bashing instances of insta-love. Eureka falls so fucking hard for Anders, despite the fact that she knows she shouldn't. Despite the fact that he lies to her. Despite the fact that he stalks her. The second time she meets Ander, he pretty much tackles her poor best friend out of no fucking where.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Then Ander lurched forward, his arm shooting over Eureka’s head. He grabbed Brooks by the neck of his T-shirt. “How long have you been with her? How long?”<br />Eureka shrank between them, startled by the outburst. What was Ander talking about? She should do something to defuse the situation. But what?</i>
</blockquote>Totally normal behavior. And whose fault is it that Ander attacks Brooks unprovoked? Why, all Brooks, of course.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Eureka pivoted to look him in the eye. “Why were you so hostile to him?”<br />“Me?” Brooks flattened a hand against his chest. “Are you serious? He—I—”<br />“You were standing over me like some possessive older brother. You could have introduced yourself.”</i>
</blockquote>WHAT? NO! Get your head on straight, girl!!!!<br /><br />There are so many instances of stalking, of irrational, dangerous, threatening behavior. Eureka questions why she's so in love with this guy who lies to her. He is suspicious. He is weird. <b>Eureka tells her instincts to shut the fuck up and leave her alone.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>She didn’t know why she was defending Ander. He’d lied about Brooks, admitted to spying on her, made vague threats about her being in danger. It might be enough to press charges, but it seemed wrong. What Ander had said wasn’t what was dangerous about him. What was dangerous about him was the way he made her feel … emotionally out of control.</i>
</blockquote><b>Get your fucking priorities straight.</b><br /><br />I really would not recommend this book unless you don't mind reading something you've probably read 100 times over. There is nothing to distinguish this book from any other YA PNR out there. Nothing. Go reread <i>Twilight</i>, I mean it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13768541139727261921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711638077" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15609104831662144066">Review also at:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2017/11/03/teardrop-lauren-kate/#more-5235'>https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress....</a><br/><br/>To put it straight this book is as dull as dirt. So... what a boring book. I was intrigued by the idea of someone having the power to cry a whole land into the sea. Then I pictured them crying all our continents in the sea due to global warming..<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386830412ra/7453265.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[It's basically a legend about Atlantis (which i was disappointed about) and how long ago two girls loved one man and when they were separated she cried Atlantis into the sea. Eureka t</span></span>
  <span id="freeText15609104831662144066" style="display:none">Review also at:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress.com/2017/11/03/teardrop-lauren-kate/#more-5235">https://edwardsghostengine.wordpress....</a><br><br>To put it straight this book is as dull as dirt. So... what a boring book. I was intrigued by the idea of someone having the power to cry a whole land into the sea. Then I pictured them crying all our continents in the sea due to global warming..<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386830412ra/7453265.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's basically a legend about Atlantis (which i was disappointed about) and how long ago two girls loved one man and when they were separated she cried Atlantis into the sea. Eureka turned out to be a descendant of Atlantis and it turned out a lot though not all of women in her line carry Selene's Tearline which means if they cry Atlantis will rise again. It turned out that throughout the generations the fallen atlanteans (which no one can locate not even the seedbearers) have been able to project their consciousness' and possess people who are close to the tearline women in hopes of upsetting them and making them cry which will bring atlantis back. Then there's Ander who is a seedbearer another escaped line from atlantis who are all connected by a higher wind/power known as the zephyr oh and they all have gills somewhere on their torsos to breathe underwater. The seedbearers see it upon themselves to carry forward the seed of atlantis' knowledge but also prevent the evils of atlantis from rising again. They saw it as the apocalypse if atlantis was to rise because according to the story atlantis was an evil place. So to stop the possibility of atlantis rising they kill every girl with the tearline but failed to kill eureka because ander saved her out of his love for her while also defying all he was led to believe and his family. In the end eureka does cry due to all the bad things that happened to her and her whole world floods. She and her friends then go in search of a lost seedbearer who left the family ages ago as it seems its up to eureka to stop the atlantean king. The book ends with Brooks eurekas best friend who is possessed by the atlantean king.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The trouble for me about this book was the fact that it started off so strong. I mean opening it from Anders point of view and giving a hint to more mysterious elements was pretty exciting. But things just went down from there. The style of writing and plot was just so uneventful and tedious, it was quite a struggle to get through this book. Most of this book up until about 100 pages from the end is just about Eureka's daily life. Even when things start happening and answers are revealed, it's still boring and unexciting. For me this just read like a long cheesy average everyday romance.<br><br>That gets me onto the characters.. yeah bottom line I hated them all. I mean Ander was as annoying and infuriating as fuck just everything about him from his insta love with eureka and his mysterious dismissive attitude just annoyed the hell out of me. But any annoyance I have for ander is minuscule compared to Eureka. I really dislike these naive love struck submissive YA heroines who refuse to properly stand up for themselves. Eureka hardly stood up to anyone who pushed her around or was unreasonable to her I mean come on girl you must have some spark of pride inside you? No? I guess the author didn't grant you even a sliver of dignity *sigh* which is the reason these characters didn't feel real to me and why I couldn't connect to them. <br><br>I would recommend this book to those who prefer their romances on the cheesy side coz did I mention that this book had some of the most cheesiest romance lines I've ever read?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_748216053" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/748216053" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/748216053?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer748216053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15199827616258562828">(Source: I own a copy of this book – why, oh why, oh why?)<br/>Eureka doesn’t cry, not ever, even when her mother dies. But she’s about to find out that she’s something awesome!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383148138ra/6416182.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So I didn’t really like ‘Fallen’, but since I’ve had some luck with sequels recently, I decided to give Lauren Kate another chance and read Teardrop. I really shouldn’t have bothered.<br/><br/>Eureka was such a whiny character. I got so sick of her moaning so quickly. She was just irritating, and whiny, and couldn’t seem to make up her </span>
  <span id="freeText15199827616258562828" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book – why, oh why, oh why?)<br>Eureka doesn’t cry, not ever, even when her mother dies. But she’s about to find out that she’s something awesome!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383148138ra/6416182.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I didn’t really like ‘Fallen’, but since I’ve had some luck with sequels recently, I decided to give Lauren Kate another chance and read Teardrop. I really shouldn’t have bothered.<br><br>Eureka was such a whiny character. I got so sick of her moaning so quickly. She was just irritating, and whiny, and couldn’t seem to make up her mind about anything. I really wanted her to just quit her moaning and shut the hell up.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383147882ra/6416077.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline was just dull. I will say that this is possibly more to do with wrong book wrong person, but this book seriously tested my resolve to finish this book. I was bored, really bored, right from the beginning, and nothing about this book really captured my attention. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380863380ra/3138624.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When things were revealed within the plot I didn’t find them exciting or impressing, the characters came out with the cheesiest lines, and the whole thing was predictable and unbelievable. Then when we found out some of the biggest secrets, they were just pants.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383148138ra/6416183.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending was also just as bad. I couldn’t quite believe what I was reading, and I really didn’t like it. We were also left with a dreaded cliff hanger. Needless to say that I won’t be reading the next book in the series.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/419967.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Overall; boring and cheesy.<br>2.5 out of 10.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15199827616258562828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4290495281047108557">I have to say that Teardrop is a GREAT book! I have been on the fence about reading this because I loved The Fallen Series and no one can take the place of Daniel and Cam but in Teardrop we have Ander and Brooks and whole lot of mythology going on. I love reading stories about Atlantis and the underwater world. This books prehistory prologue started out strong and the book for me got stronger. The ending had me screaming because I needed more I needed about three chapters more but I will have to</span>
  <span id="freeText4290495281047108557" style="display:none">I have to say that Teardrop is a GREAT book! I have been on the fence about reading this because I loved The Fallen Series and no one can take the place of Daniel and Cam but in Teardrop we have Ander and Brooks and whole lot of mythology going on. I love reading stories about Atlantis and the underwater world. This books prehistory prologue started out strong and the book for me got stronger. The ending had me screaming because I needed more I needed about three chapters more but I will have to wait to see what happens.<br /><br />Can you imagine being told all your life you could not cry? Man I think I would die because crying is a natural part of life but for Eureka she can't cry because her mother told her she couldn't. Then an accident takes Eurekas mother and she is left all alone except for her best friend Brooks and a few trinkets her mother has left behind. Plus Eureka has Ander who is a little weird because he tells her things and she just doesn't believe them. But in all Ander's weirdness what he has told Eureka so far has been the truth and she is learning to trust him.<br /><br />Armed with what her mother left her which was a locket, letter, stone, and ancient book Eureka must figure out why her mother left her all this stuff. She will have to figure out what these things do but she will learn that everyone around her is not who they are and things are definitely about to get strange for Eureka and she will have to follow her heart. Who will she love? Who will be there for her? She will see just how much Brooks loves her and how much they mean to one another. She will also learn how much Ander loves her and how much he is willing to sacrifice to save her from the evil that lurks below. </span>

<div id="review_952836280" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952836280" />
    <a title="Laurel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7421701-laurel"><img alt="Laurel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514649429p2/7421701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952836280?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel" href="/user/show/7421701-laurel">Laurel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952836280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13090618095661532037">WHY do we still have stalkerish boys?? Why the sexism? Why this whiny and ungrateful protagonist? WHY THE SLUT-SHAMING? *loud clear coughing* Girls, not every girl you meet needs to be degraded just to prove how SPECIAL or whatever you are.<br/><br/>Yeah, no. Once upon a time, I read Fallen by Lauren Kate. I was forced to DNF it after I chucked it across the room because of its rampant sexism, Luce's whining and the grossness from the male characters. But I'm not one to give up on an author just because o</span>
  <span id="freeText13090618095661532037" style="display:none">WHY do we still have stalkerish boys?? Why the sexism? Why this whiny and ungrateful protagonist? WHY THE SLUT-SHAMING? *loud clear coughing* Girls, not every girl you meet needs to be degraded just to prove how SPECIAL or whatever you are.<br /><br />Yeah, no. Once upon a time, I read Fallen by Lauren Kate. I was forced to DNF it after I chucked it across the room because of its rampant sexism, Luce's whining and the grossness from the male characters. But I'm not one to give up on an author just because of one book! So I requested to read this book to see if it's better. Yet, here we are again with a whiny, ungrateful protagonist, rampant sexism , slut-shaming and general grossness from the male characters.<br /><br />Okay, let me be positive first. The writing isn't bad. It's quite visual and pretty. The premise is a little eyebrow-raising, but Atlantis? Hey, that's pretty cool! The cover of this book is gorgeous. That's probably what seduced me to check if out.<br /><br />But, seriously, what the hell. <br />So Teardrop kicks off with a prologue written from Ander's perspective. He tells you everything you need to know about the kind of book this is but, I was still hopeful. We learn that he has been watching a girl his entire life and now he is in love with her. But because of his otherworldly nature, of course he must have THE choice: save the world or save the girl. <br /><br />Then we meet Eureka (this name, really?). And boy, is she whiny and ungrateful. Eureka thinks she has the right to be awful, rude and outright vile to anyone she comes in contact with. She is horrible to her therapist, a woman only trying to make her feel better, and she treats her family like trash. Her attitude towards her stepmother was embarrassing. She also degrades and slut-shames every female character she sees. Her own friend isn't free from her judgement. But, I can't even hate her because she was so bland. She didn't leave an impression on me that could make me feel something as as strongly as hate.<br /><br />The rest of the characters were one dimensional. The stepmother was ridiculous. We were supposed to hate her so she was evil to the extent of being a caricature. I mean she made Eureka pay for her own therapy after she tried to commit suicide! The dad was pathetic. He had absolutely no backbone and was bullied and swayed by all the women in his life. I <br />I feel sorry for Cat because her best friend is horrible. Brooks was my favourite for a while, but even he wasn't quite himself.<br /><br />The romance was as predicted. Creepy and cheesy. Ander was stalking Eureka and so he fell in love with her. Or rather, he became obsessed. Then he continues to stalk her and she now knows this but she's drawn to him and blah blah eternal love "I will let the world end for you". I was genuinely shocked that books like this are still coming out. <br /><br />Nothing happens for 80%of the book and when things start happening it's still very boring. The mythology was kinda cool but hey, when you have the narration focused on Eureka, even that's not interesting. <br /><br />Things happen and the end comes and I congratulated myself for at least reaching the ending. This is the kind of book I would have expected during the Fallen era. I may have liked it back then too (but I hated Fallen, so). But seriously, nope. This wasn't even my cup of tea. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13090618095661532037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_794901106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794901106" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794901106?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857532275" href="/book/show/16069600-teardrop">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">you shouldn't</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794901106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1545688647691944533"><b>I'm thoroughly disappointed..</b><br/><br/>I'm surprised I didn't give this an one-star rating but thought "let's save it for the next book" because I'm sure the next one will be even worse. After 2 hours of writing the review the idea of changing the rating got a hold on me. So, here I am giving it 1 star. Oops.<br/><br/>While in this book the plot is really intriguing, or it could be, if it had the right author, it gets very annoying and boring several times. I'm not a huge fan of Lauren Kate's writing. Her writing i</span>
  <span id="freeText1545688647691944533" style="display:none"><b>I'm thoroughly disappointed..</b><br /><br />I'm surprised I didn't give this an one-star rating but thought "let's save it for the next book" because I'm sure the next one will be even worse. After 2 hours of writing the review the idea of changing the rating got a hold on me. So, here I am giving it 1 star. Oops.<br /><br />While in this book the plot is really intriguing, or it could be, if it had the right author, it gets very annoying and boring several times. I'm not a huge fan of Lauren Kate's writing. Her writing in 'Fallen' varied from 'mediocre' to 'good' but in this one it's like while writing this she forgot to use her skills.<br /><br />The characters were annoying, all of them, most of all Eureka.. What kind of name is this? Eureka is the typical headstrong, independent girl who just can't help getting on your nerves. She is a complete fetus. She acts like the entire universe is in an orbit around her. She also cannot cry, not now, not ever. Well, that could have been interesting but I figured out why by the first 50 pages so it ruined the entire book because I had nothing to anticipate for.<br /><br />Mrs. Kate also tried to play her love-triangle card again but failed altogether. And something tells me that she's not done with the love-triangle thingy and in the second book there'll be more of it.<br /><br />Now, for the male leads. They both are the epitome of beauty.. That's a first. LOL. If I were to say who I liked best, I'd answer Ander because he's kind of mysterious and more down-to-earth but then again we didn't see the real Brooks at all so I can't tell for sure.<br /><br />Can we take a minute to applause for the fact that Mrs. Kate tried to pull many similar cards she had pulled in the 'Fallen' series?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. Love-triangle.. Both boys tried to get her attention for different reasons.<br />2. She chose the most mysterious one.<br />3. The heroine was the center of the world for everyone.<br />4. Many similar scenes, including that one in the pond. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Thanks for reading my review! Will I be reading the second book? Probably yes because I'm a masochist. Do I recommend this to you? Hell to the no.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1545688647691944533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber  ~ The Reading Addict" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber  ~ The Reading Addict" href="/user/show/3172251-amber-the-reading-addict">Amber  ~ The Reading Addict</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer534495696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2735609022874160851">I'll be honest: I picked this book up solely because of the cover. LOOK AT HER WATER DRESS. I couldn't not find out what that was all about. I also knew of Lauren Kate's previous works and figured it would be an interesting read. <br/><br/>The premise is unique. Lost underwater civilizations and romance? Count me in. Kate possesses a creative style and confidently weaves vivid images. However, I will say that some of her descriptions go a little too far. Jammed packed with metaphors and adjectives, her ph</span>
  <span id="freeText2735609022874160851" style="display:none">I'll be honest: I picked this book up solely because of the cover. LOOK AT HER WATER DRESS. I couldn't not find out what that was all about. I also knew of Lauren Kate's previous works and figured it would be an interesting read. <br /><br />The premise is unique. Lost underwater civilizations and romance? Count me in. Kate possesses a creative style and confidently weaves vivid images. However, I will say that some of her descriptions go a little too far. Jammed packed with metaphors and adjectives, her phrases often left me a little winded. <br /><br />Each of the characters has a defined personality. Eureka is the confused, deep girl who no one understands. Cat is the spunky flirt of a friend girls wish they had. Then there are the two boys... Honestly, a bit of an eye roll there. One is the best friend, one is the mysterious stranger who Eureka can't help but be attracted to. Gee, never seen that before. The whole I've-known-you-your-whole-life thing is getting just a little old. I've never been a fan of insta-romance. <br /><br />It's not that I didn't enjoy Teardrop. I just hoped for more originality. The plot was a little drawn out and could easily have been so much more. Love triangles aren't as entertaining as they used to be. Not sure if I'll check out the sequels. Maybe I'll give the second one a chance if the cover is as cool... (I'm shallow, I know). </span>
  <a data-text-id="2735609022874160851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It makes me very angry , specially because I was warned about this book and that I won't like it , but I didn't listen. <br/><br/>So the first thin</span>
  <span id="freeText10917157917825289243" style="display:none">WTF did I just read?<br />This is by far THE WORST book I read this year. There are so many things that I hate about it so I don't even know where to start. <br />Let's just start from the fact that it took me five days to read it , which would also make it my longest read this year , so I can't even think of the time I waisted on it , when I could of read something else. It makes me very angry , specially because I was warned about this book and that I won't like it , but I didn't listen. <br /><br />So the first thing that makes this book SO BAD is... I just can't actually decide between the characters and "the plot". I really don't know what is worse. <br /><br />The plot: It was dull , already seen , unbelivably predictible ( funny story: I actually figured it out almost at the beginning , which is very sad) . Overall nothing original or interesting .<br />Then we've got the characters who I wanted to kill throughout the hall book. They were all so annoying and badly developed. I just can't even count how many times I rolled my eyes while reading it. Relationships between the characters were absoulutly ridiculess and their conversation were just ugh. <br />I don't even want to start on the insta love - I feel like I've known you my entire life- I just got one look at you and I already love you - you're obviously my soulmate thing. NO , NO and NO . Why do people do that??? I hate it from the bottom of my heart. Is it supposed to be cute , am I supose to ship them now?? No way. I just don't understand how can you love someone or feel like you can trust them after you bearly have spoken few times. Specially if that person seems like a creepy stalkeer who happens to know all about your life. I mean Ander and Eureka were just the worst couple ever. <br />Than there's this hall love triangle thing . *Rolling my eyes* I don't really hate love triangles , but they can pass only if they are convicible , which was so not the case in this book. <br />One of the main problems with this book is of course how BORING to death it was. It has like about 400 hundred pages of literally nothing happening. No plot , no fun , no action , just main character whining about how awful her life is , how nobody understands her , how her family is terrible and how evil her stepmother is. BORING.<br />I actually skipped a lot of pages because I saw nothing was happening which I never do or did . I wanted to read Lauren Kate's Fallen series , but I don't think I'll do it . Although it seemed nice .<br />I'm definitly not reading second part.<br /></span>

    <a title="Aiman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16076980-aiman"><img alt="Aiman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405936664p2/16076980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/544821686?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aiman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aiman" href="/user/show/16076980-aiman">Aiman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=y-a-rom">y-a-rom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=kill-me-now">kill-me-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=myth">myth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=drab-and-drag">drab-and-drag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=awesome-covers">awesome-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544821686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10202363295715676052">Well, well, well. What do we have here? Why, it is yet another vague and tedious romance by Lauren Kate. Surprise, surprise. Who would've guessed right?<br/><br/>Teardrop is about- well, I'm sure you've already guessed. A 'special' girl, who apparently is destined to do great things. A 'mysterious' stalker whom she feels 'strangely attracted' to. Her funny and understanding best friend. Stalker dude's family who wants to kill her but then stalker dude daringly defies his family *sarcastic gasp* to save hi</span>
  <span id="freeText10202363295715676052" style="display:none">Well, well, well. What do we have here? Why, it is yet another vague and tedious romance by Lauren Kate. Surprise, surprise. Who would've guessed right?<br /><br />Teardrop is about- well, I'm sure you've already guessed. A 'special' girl, who apparently is destined to do great things. A 'mysterious' stalker whom she feels 'strangely attracted' to. Her funny and understanding best friend. Stalker dude's family who wants to kill her but then stalker dude daringly defies his family *sarcastic gasp* to save his true love. Sound familiar?<br /><br />Half of the plot was so stereotypical and clichéd that I wasn't even bothered to roll my eyes. The other half <i>sounded</i> half-promising but was completely ambiguous, in <i>true</i> Lauren Kate style. The characters were incessantly annoying and I was constantly being bored to tears.<br /><br />Eureka Boudreaux's (that name...) mother is killed by a rogue wave as the daughter and mother are driving on a bridge. Miraculously, (yeah, right) she is left alive, with only broken wrists and a deaf left ear. Eureka is left devastated and even attempts suicide. <i>Her suicide attempt is totally unintentional of course, because there is no way there can be a protagonist who is genuinely of an unstable mind. Of course not.</i><br /><br />Eureka is left mourning only with a compelling mystery and aching heart and her best friend is acting strange. She has a 'beautiful stalker' and must deal with her adolescent life. How tragic. <b>NOT.</b><br /><br /><u>Eureka:</u> (Am I the only one who doesn't understand the story of how she got her name?) I can't make up my mind about her. I can try and emphatize with her loss but her personality isn't very appealing. I hope nobody looks to her as a heroine or role model. Eureka was overly whiny, ungrateful and just plain irritating. What I mean, is that if I wanted to read petulant complaints from a hormonal teenager, I would simply read my own diary entries or conversed with that whinging girl from school.<br /><br /><u>Ander:</u> He was supposed to be the main male protagonist but he was hardly in the book at all. He was all shadowy and dodgy yet Eureka kissed him like, two minutes after he entered her bedroom- without permission, 'cause apparently he's a badass rebel like that.<br /><br />Ugh, writing this review is evoking violent fits of annoyance and rage or maybe it's just me. I am in urgent need of a kilo of chocolate or a litre of ice-cream.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10202363295715676052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
